Checkpoint
What does Nasafi argue would happen if God became a Creator only at the moment of creation?
A) God would be more perfect than before
B) God would be dependent on creation and subject to change
C) The world would become eternal
D) Takwin would be a created thing

Key Takeaway
Denying the eternity of takwin forces the absurd conclusion that God is dependent and changeable, which contradicts His perfection.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever find yourself relying on the praise of others to feel complete? How does Nasafi's argument that need is a deficiency expose the spiritual danger in that? Will you consciously turn to God alone for approval today?
?
If even a single change in God would make Him contingent, what does that say about your own constant changes in mood, intention, and character? When you change, do you recognize your own createdness and need for the Unchanging One?
?
The argument says that if God needed creation to be praised, He would be imperfect. Are you living as though God needs your worship, or as though you need His mercy? How does this lesson reshape your motive for prayer?

The Deficiency Argument: God Cannot Be Temporally Deficient
First argument against God becoming a creator in time: deficiency implies temporality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the claim that God becomes a creator after not being one implies that God was deficient in pre-eternity, which leads to the impossibility of temporality in the Eternal.

Core Idea
Deficiency is a sign of temporality—it cannot be attributed to the Eternal.

This lesson examines the first argument in the refutation: the claim that God becomes a creator implies He was more deficient before creation. The author demonstrates that deficiency is a mark of temporal origination, so attributing it to God would lead to the absurd conclusion that the Eternal is temporal.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Identify the premise that deficiency is a sign of temporality.
The author uses a reductio ad absurdum argument.
2
Understand the implication
Notice that if God were more deficient before, then pre-eternal deficiency would imply temporal origination. That would make the Eternal temporal, which is impossible.
3
Reflect on the conclusion
Ask yourself: why is it impossible for the pre-eternal to be temporal? This is a basic axiom in kalam.
This argument defends God's absolute perfection in pre-eternity.

Source Text

يجعله خالقا بارئا مصورا في الأزل، فقد زعم أن الله تعالى في الأزل كان أنقص منه الآن، والنقص من أمارات الحدث، فإذا ثبت في القدم دليل حدوث الله تعالى جل ربنا عن ذلك، فكان الله تعالى على زعم هذا القائل في الأزل محدثا، وكون الأزلي محدثا محال . وكون ذات واحد محدثا قديما ممتنع - ولأنه لو صار خالق يخلق حادث لصار بموجود المخلوقات ممدوحا فحصل له التمدح بغيره لا بنفسه، فكان محتاجا إلى وجود ذلك الغير ليدفع به نقصه، إذ الحاجة ليست إلا نقصا يرتفع بالمطلوب وينجبر به ولأنه لو كان كذلك لصار بفعله جالبا إلى نفسه نفعا مكتسبا ما يستفيد به مدحا ورفعة وكمال درجة وجلال قدر، وهذا كله من أمارات الحاجة ودلائل النقص وسمات الحدوث، وكل محدث مخلوق لا خالق، فإذا كان الخالق عندهم مخلوقا، ولأنه تعالى لو لم يكن خالقا ثم صار خالقا وقد مر أن استحقاقه الوصف إما أن يكون بصفة قائمة بالذات أو بصفة راجعة إلى الذات، وصفة الخلق ليست براجعة إلى ذاته بل هي وراء ذاته بالإجماع، فلو لم تكن قائمة بالذات لم يكن مستحقا اسم الخالق بها على ما بينا، ثم إذا صار خالقا صار لقيامه به فيصير متغيرا عند صيرورته خالقا إذ الذات بحدوث صفة فيه لم تكن ثابتة يتغير عما كان عليه، والتغير من أمارات الحدوث، فإذا يصير مخلوقا عند صيرورته خالقا، وصار من يعبد الخالق عابد المخلوق، وهذا كله محال. والذي يحققه أن من يجوز عليه الفعل لا ينتفي عنه الفعل إلا عن عجز.
He makes Him a Creator, a Maker, a Formator in pre-eternity, for he claimed that Allah Most High in pre-eternity was more deficient than He is now, and deficiency is a sign of temporal origination. So if in pre-eternity a proof of the temporal origination of Allah is established—exalted is our Lord above that—then Allah Most High, according to this claimant, would be temporal in pre-eternity, and the notion of the pre-eternal being temporal is impossible. And it is impossible for one essence to be both temporal and eternal. And because if He were to become a Creator who creates a temporal thing, He would become praised through the existence of creatures, so He would obtain praise from other than Himself, not from Himself. Thus He would be in need of the existence of that other to remove His deficiency, for need is nothing but a deficiency that is removed by the needed thing and compensated by it. And because if it were so, He would by His act attract benefit to Himself, acquiring praise, elevation, perfection of degree, and majesty of rank. And all of this is of the signs of need, indications of deficiency, and marks of temporality. And every temporal thing is created, not creator. Thus if the Creator according to them is created, and because if He Most High were not a Creator and then became a Creator, and it has been established that His deserving the description is either by an attribute subsisting in the Essence or by an attribute referring back to the Essence, and the attribute of creation does not refer back to His Essence but is outside His Essence by consensus, so if it were not subsisting in the Essence, He would not deserve the name 'Creator' by it, as we have explained. Then when He becomes a Creator, He becomes due to its subsistence in Him, so He would change upon becoming a Creator, because the Essence, by the occurrence of an attribute in it, is not stable and changes from what it was. And change is of the signs of temporality. Thus He would become created when He becomes a Creator, and the one who worships the Creator becomes a worshiper of the created. And all of this is impossible. And what establishes it is that one for whom action is possible does not refrain from action except due to incapacity.
Source pages p. 553

Commentary
This passage refutes the view that God becomes a Creator after not being one, arguing that it leads to multiple absurdities. The author begins by stating the claim that God in pre-eternity was more deficient than after creation, which is impossible because deficiency is a sign of temporal origination. If God were temporal in pre-eternity, the pre-eternal would be temporal—a contradiction. Next, the author argues that if God were to become a Creator through creation, He would be praised for something other than Himself, indicating need. Need is a deficiency that requires an external object. If God's act of creating brought Him benefit such as praise and exaltation, He would be dependent on creation, which cannot be attributed to God. Additionally, if His being a Creator were a new attribute, it would either be intrinsic or relational. Since creation is not relational (by consensus), it must be intrinsic, causing change in the divine Essence. Change is a sign of temporality, so God would be created when He becomes Creator, making worship of the Creator actually worship of a created being. Finally, the author states a general principle: if action is possible for an agent, the absence of action indicates incapacity—thus denying eternal creativity implies incapacity in God. This refutation defends the Maturidi position that the attribute of takwin is eternal.

Key Terms

البارئ
المصور
الأزل
النقص
الحدث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that God's becoming creator does not imply deficiency, but the author argues that if He gains a new attribute, He was previously lacking it, which is deficiency.
Correction: God's attributes are eternal; any new attribution would imply change and need.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does deficiency indicate?
A) Perfection
B) Temporal origination
C) Eternity
D) Need

Key Takeaway
Any deficiency in God undermines His eternity; thus the claim that He becomes a creator implies a prior deficiency that is impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever, even subconsciously, thought that Allah needed your worship or that your actions added something to His perfection? This lesson shows that any such thought implies deficiency in Him. Examine your heart: do you truly believe Allah is perfectly independent, needing nothing? If not, repent and affirm His absolute self-sufficiency.
?
When you face a difficulty, do you ever feel that Allah has changed toward you or that He is not as merciful as before? The argument here refutes any notion of change in Allah. Reflect on a time you doubted Allah's constancy, and commit to trusting His eternal attributes.
?
The passage argues that deficiency is a sign of being created. In what ways do you still attribute human-like limitations to Allah in your mind? Identify one subtle assumption you hold about Allah that undermines His perfection, and resolve to correct it using the teaching of this lesson.

The Need and Praise Argument: God Cannot Depend on Creation
Second argument: becoming a creator implies need and dependence on creation for praise.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the claim that God becomes a creator implies that God needs creation to be praised, which contradicts His self-sufficiency.

Core Idea
If God needs creation to be praised, He is dependent—impossible for the Independent.

The second argument focuses on the fact that if God becomes a creator through His act, He would be praised for something external to Himself. This would mean He needs creation to remove a deficiency, which is incompatible with divine perfection.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the passage starting from 'ولأنه لو صار خالق' to 'كل محدث مخلوق لا خالق'. Note the logical flow: if He becomes a creator, He is praised through creatures; that implies need.
2
Understand the praise argument
The author argues that if God's praise comes from His creation, then He depends on that creation. Need is a deficiency, and deficiency is a sign of temporality.
The passage lists multiple consequences: need, benefit, signs of temporality.
3
Identify the conclusion
The passage concludes that if the Creator is temporal, then He is created, not Creator—a contradiction.
This is a powerful reduction.

The Change Argument and Principle of Capacity
Third and fourth arguments: change in Essence and the principle of capacity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the claim that God becomes a creator entails change in the divine Essence, which is a sign of temporality, and why refraining from creation would imply incapacity.

Core Idea
Any new attribute in God would change His Essence, impossible for the Unchanging.

The third and fourth arguments address the issue of change. If God's being a creator is a new attribute, it would either be relational or intrinsic. Since it is not relational, it must be intrinsic, causing change in the Essence. Change is a sign of temporality. Additionally, if God can create but refrains, that would imply incapacity, so eternal creativity is necessary.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read from 'ولأنه تعالى لو لم يكن خالقا' to the end. Focus on the distinction between relational and intrinsic attributes.
2
Analyze the change argument
The author says the attribute of creation is not relational (by consensus), so it must be intrinsic. If it were to occur in time, it would change the Essence. Change implies temporality.
This leads to the conclusion that God would become created when becoming Creator.
3
Understand the final principle
The last sentence asserts that if action is possible for an agent, the absence of action indicates incapacity. So if God were able to create but did not, He would be incapable—impossible. Thus, His creativity is eternal.
This completes the refutation.

Logical Proof for the Eternity of Takwin Through Division
Nasafi presents a logical proof using division for takwin's eternity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the method of division (qisma) is used in kalam to prove that the divine attribute of takwin is eternal and necessarily subsisting in God's essence.

Core Idea
When all alternatives are impossible, the remaining one is necessarily true.

This lesson presents a concise logical argument from Imam al-Nasafi's Tabṣirat al-Adilla. Using the method of division, he establishes the eternity of takwin—the attribute of bringing into existence. The argument is a model of kalam reasoning: it eliminates impossible scenarios to arrive at the necessary conclusion. Let's examine the logic step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the translation to get a preliminary understanding of the argument.
2
Understand the general logical principle
Identify the two conditional statements that form the general rule: when all divisions are impossible, the remaining one is determined; and when divisions are equal and one is necessary, that one is affirmed.
Notice the terms: possibility (imkan), necessity (wujub), and affirmation (thubut).
3
Apply to the case of takwin
See how Nasafi applies the principle: in the case of takwin, all divisions except one are impossible, so the remaining division is necessarily established.
The conclusion is that takwin is eternal and subsisting in God's essence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الدلائل الاستقرائية إذا امتنعت الأقسام كلها وتعين قسم للإمكان تعين للثبوت، ولو استوت الأقسام في الإمكان وتعين قسم للوجوب كان هو المتعين للثبوت لرجحانه على غيره من الأقسام، فإذا امتنعت الأقسام كلها فيما نحن فيه وتعين القسم الباقي للوجوب كان هو الثابت ضرورة.
Inductive proofs: if all the divisions are impossible and a division is determined for possibility, it is determined for affirmation; and if the divisions are equal in possibility and a division is determined for necessity, then it is determined for affirmation due to its preponderance over other divisions. So if all the divisions are impossible in our subject and the remaining division is determined for necessity, then it is necessarily established.
Source pages p. 554

Commentary
This passage is a logical proof using the method of division (qisma). The author, Imam al-Nasafi, states a general principle: in inductive reasoning, when all possible divisions or alternatives are impossible except one, that remaining one is necessarily proven. He then applies this to the attribute of takwin (bringing into existence) to show that it must be eternal and subsisting in God's essence. The argument follows a standard kalam method of eliminating impossible alternatives to arrive at the necessary conclusion.

Key Terms
تكوين
الدلائل الاستقرائية
الأقسام
إمكان
وجوب
ثبوت
ضرورة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The proof is circular because it assumes the conclusion at the start.
Correction: The proof is not circular; it eliminates impossible alternatives without assuming the conclusion. The conclusion follows necessarily from the elimination of all impossible divisions.

Checkpoint
What is the logical principle used to prove the eternity of takwin?
A) Direct textual evidence from the Quran
B) When all divisions are impossible except one, that one is necessarily established
C) Analogy with created beings
D) Consensus of the Salaf

Key Takeaway
The method of division shows that takwin must be eternal because all other alternatives are impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This proof eliminates all alternatives to arrive at the truth about God's attribute. What alternatives do you keep alive in your life that prevent you from submitting fully to the truth about yourself and your Lord? Will you eliminate them today?
?
The passage shows that takwin is eternally in God's essence—His act of creation is not an afterthought. Does your prayer life reflect a deep trust in an eternal, ever-active God, or do you treat Him as distant until you urgently need Him? How will you change your daily worship to acknowledge His constant creative power?
?
The proof relies on the impossibility of certain divisions. What 'impossible' spiritual state have you made peace with—like persisting in a sin or avoiding repentance—that, if you faced it honestly, would collapse and force you to affirm the only remaining alternative: turning back to Allah with no excuse? What step will you take this week to act on that necessity?

Eternal Attributes: Defending Abu Hanifa's Creed
Nasafi explains and defends Abu Hanifa's statement on eternal attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Abu Hanifa's statement 'He has not ceased with His attributes' affirms the eternity of God's attributes and why accusing him of innovation is unfounded.

Core Idea
God's attributes are eternal; creation adds nothing to His essence.

Nasafi begins by quoting Abu Hanifa's foundational statement on divine attributes, which affirms that God's attributes are eternal and not acquired through creation. He then clarifies a potential misinterpretation and provides a logical proof. This lesson unpacks the argument and explains why this creed is immune to accusations of innovation.

Guided Path
1
Read the quote from al-ʿAqāʾid
Read the opening quote where Abu Hanifa states that God has not ceased with His attributes, eternal before creation. Observe the precise phrasing.
Notice the phrase 'lam yazdad' (did not increase) – it is key.
2
Understand the clarification
Nasafi explains that 'before His creation' means before all created things, and the negation of increase proves God's attributes are not temporal.
He contrasts 'by their coming into existence' with 'by His coming into existence'.
3
Reflect on the defense
Consider the concluding argument: given Abu Hanifa's stature and knowledge, his doctrine cannot be dismissed as innovation. Note the appeal to history and scholarship.
This shows the gravity of misattributing innovation to early scholars.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسمى بالعقائد الذي افتتحه فقال: صح عندي مذهب فقهاء الملة أبي حنيفة النعمان بن ثابت الكوفي وأبي يوسف يعقوب بن إبراهيم الأنصاري وأبي عبد الله محمد بن الحسن الشيباني ثم شرع في بيان أقاويلهم إلى أن قال: وما زال بصفاته قديما قبل خلقه ولم يزدد بكونهم شيئا لم يكن قبلهم من صفته ثم قال: له معنى الربوبية ولا مربوب ومعنى الخالقية ولا مخلوق، وأراد بقوله: قبل خلقه أي قبل مخلوقاته، ألا ترى أنه قال: ولم يزدد بكونهم شيئا ولم يقل بكونه، ولأنه لو أراد به صفة الخلق لم يقل لم يزدد، وفي هذا أيضا إشارة إلى الدليل في المسألة، بينا أنه لا يجوز أن يستفيد بالمخلوقين صفة مدح. وإن قولا كان أبو حنيفة وكبار أصحابه قائلين به مع تبحرهم في أنواع العلوم وتقدم زمانهم، لحقيق أن لا ينسب إلى الحدوث بعد الأربعمائة من سني الهجرة وجهالة من نسبه إلى ذلك ظاهرة.
The one called 'al-ʿAqāʾid' which he opened saying: 'The madhhab of the jurists of the community – Abu Hanifa al-Nuʿman ibn Thabit al-Kufi, Abu Yusuf Yaʿqub ibn Ibrahim al-Ansari, and Abu ʿAbdillah Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani – is correct according to me.' Then he began explaining their statements until he said: 'He has not ceased (to be) with His attributes, eternal before His creation, and He did not increase by their coming into existence anything that was not of His attribute before them.' Then he said: 'He has the meaning of Lordship with no lorded, and the meaning of Creatorhood with no created.' And he meant by His saying 'before His creation' – i.e., before His created things. Do you not see that he said: 'and He did not increase by their coming into existence anything' and did not say 'by His coming into existence'? And because if he had intended the attribute of creation, he would not have said 'did not increase.' And in this also is an indication of the proof on the issue: we have clarified that it is not permissible that He should acquire from creatures an attribute of praise. And a saying that Abu Hanifa and his major companions held, with their deep knowledge in the types of sciences and the precedence of their time, is worthy not to be attributed to origination (al-ḥudūth) after four hundred years of the Hijra, and the ignorance of one who attributes that to him is apparent.
Source pages p. 555

Commentary
This passage is a theological defense and explanation of Abu Hanifa's creed. It begins by quoting from the work 'al-ʿAqāʾid', where Abu Hanifa affirms the eternal attributes of God with the phrase 'He has not ceased (to be) with His attributes, eternal before His creation.' The author clarifies that 'before His creation' means before all created things. He then draws attention to the phrase 'did not increase,' arguing that if God did not acquire any new attribute through creation, this disproves the idea that His attributes are temporal. The argument proceeds: if Abu Hanifa had meant the attribute of creation (as a temporal event), he would not have said 'did not increase.' The passage then states that this very reasoning serves as a proof that God cannot gain new attributes of praise from creatures. Finally, the author defends Abu Hanifa and his disciples – leaders of their time in knowledge – asserting that their doctrine cannot be accused of innovation (ḥudūth) after four centuries of Islamic history, and that anyone who makes such an accusation is manifestly ignorant.

Correction: Nasafi clarifies that 'before His creation' means before all created things, and the phrase 'did not increase' proves that no new attribute is acquired; therefore, the attributes are eternal.

Key Takeaway

The Eternity of Takwin Does Not Imply Eternal Created Things
Nasafi refutes that eternal takwin entails eternal created things.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the eternity of the divine attribute takwin does not necessitate the eternity of the created things.

Core Idea
Eternal cause does not make its effect eternal; dependence entails contingency.

Nasafi confronts a common objection: if God's power to create (takwin) is eternal, then the things He creates must also be eternal. This seems logical at first glance, but Nasafi shows it rests on a confusion about causality and the meaning of 'eternal'. In this passage, he refutes the objection by clarifying that anything whose existence depends on another is necessarily contingent.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage carefully, then read the English translation. Try to grasp the overall argument before diving into analysis.
Pay attention to the terms qadim (eternal) and hadith (contingent).
2
Identify key concepts
Identify the key terms: takwin (the act of bringing into existence), mukawwan (created thing), qadim (eternal), hadith (contingent), istighna (independence), ta‘alluq al-wujud (dependence of existence). Understand each term's role in the argument.
3
Follow Nasafi's argument
Trace Nasafi's reasoning: He starts by expressing astonishment at the objection, then states that anything dependent on a cause is contingent, not eternal. He defines the eternal as independent in existence. Since the mukawwan depends on takwin, it must be contingent. Thus the objection fails.
Notice how he uses the principle: dependence on another implies contingency.
4
Connect to broader kalam debate
Nasafi links this to the argument against the eternity of the world. Those who claim the world is eternal because its cause (God's essence or attribute) is eternal are contradictory, because the world depends on that cause.
He cites Ibn Qals to highlight the self-contradiction of claiming both eternity and a Maker.
5
Reflect on the misconception
Consider why someone might mistakenly think an eternal attribute implies eternal effects. Reflect on how understanding 'dependence' is key to avoiding this error.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قدم التكوين لا يؤدي إلى قدم المكونات: ثم العجب كل العجب أن قوما يدعون الفراهة في علم الكلام والتبحر في معرفة الدلائل يزعمون أن القول بقدم التكوين يؤدي إلى القول بقدم المكونات، مع علمهم أن ما تعلق وجوده بسبب من الأسباب فهو المحدث لا القديم، لأن القديم هو المستغني في وجوده عن غيره، فما لم يستغن عن غيره وتعلق وجوده به كان محدثا ضرورة، والمكون وجوده بالتكوين فكيف يكون قديما؟. يحقق هذا: أنا جميعا ندعي على القائلين بقدم العالم المعللين لذلك بقدم ما تعلق وجود العالم به من ذات الباري أو صفة من صفاته المناقضة حيث ادعوا قدمه مع تعلق وجوده بغيره، وهذا الذي قرن هذا القول بمقاله ابن قلس قال في الرد عليه: أنكرنا قوله لأنه قول متناقض في نفسه، لأنه بقوله العالم قديم، ينفي أن يكون له صانع ويقوله: له صانع ينفي أن يكون قديما.
The eternity of takwin (bringing into existence) does not lead to the eternity of the created things (mukawwanat): Then amazing, utterly amazing, that a people who claim skill in kalam and profound knowledge of proofs claim that the statement of the eternity of takwin leads to the statement of the eternity of the created things, despite their knowledge that whatever existence is attached to a cause among causes is contingent, not eternal. Because the eternal is independent in its existence from other than itself. So what is not independent of other than itself and its existence is attached to it is necessarily contingent. And the created thing (mukawwan) has its existence through takwin, so how can it be eternal? This is verified by [the fact that] we all argue against those who claim the eternity of the world and justify it by the eternity of that to which the existence of the world is attached—either the essence of the Creator or one of His attributes— contradictorily claiming its eternity while its existence depends on another. And this one who associated this statement with his speech Ibn Qals said in refutation: 'We reject his statement because it is contradictory in itself, for by his statement 'the world is eternal' he denies that it has a Maker, and by his statement 'it has a Maker' he denies that it is eternal.'
Source pages p. 562

Commentary
This passage refutes a specific objection. Nasafi expresses astonishment at those who claim expertise in kalam yet argue that the eternity of the attribute of takwin (God's effective power to bring things into existence) necessarily implies that the objects brought into existence (mukawwanat) are also eternal. Nasafi points out that they already know that anything whose existence depends on a cause is contingent (hadith), not eternal (qadim). The eternal is that which is independent of others for its existence. Since mukawwanat depend on takwin for their existence, they must be contingent. Thus the objection is invalid. He then connects this to the classical argument against the eternity of the world: those who claim the world is eternal because its cause (God's essence or attribute) is eternal are contradicting themselves, because dependence on another entails contingency. He cites Ibn Qals (likely a reference to a philosopher) who states that claiming the world is eternal while also claiming a Maker is self-contradictory, as the world would then be both eternal and need a Maker simultaneously.

Key Terms

المكونات
القديم
المحدث
الاستغناء
تعلق الوجود
ابن قلس
تناقض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the eternal attribute of takwin makes the created world eternal.
Correction: The created world's existence depends on takwin, so it is contingent (hadith), not eternal (qadim). Dependence on another implies contingency.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, why can the mukawwan (created thing) not be eternal?
A) Because it depends on takwin for its existence
B) Because it is material
C) Because it is not independent of time
D) Because it is multiple

Key Takeaway
An eternal attribute like takwin does not make its objects eternal; dependence on another always implies contingency.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever find yourself relying on created things—your health, wealth, or loved ones—as if they were eternal, forgetting that everything dependent on a cause is contingent and may vanish? How can you shift your trust to the Independent (al-Qadim) today?
?
Nasafi expresses astonishment at those who claim expertise yet contradict themselves. When you reflect on your own understanding of Allah’s attributes, are you willing to dig deeper to avoid such contradictions, or are you satisfied with surface-level knowledge?
?
Your very existence depends on Allah every moment, just as the mukawwan depends on takwin. Does this truth make you feel fragile and accountable, or does it drive you to sincere gratitude and reliance on Him alone? What is one specific way you can live out this dependency today?

The Karamiyya Dilemma: Qudra and Takwin
Author refutes the Karamiyya via a dilemma on qudra and takwin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author uses a logical dilemma to refute the Karamiyya position on the relationship between qudra and takwin.

Core Idea
A dilemma traps the Karamiyya: either qudra is originated or pre-eternal, both lead to absurdities.

The Karamiyya claimed that takwin is an originated attribute in God's essence, attached to qudra. The author poses a critical question: is qudra itself pre-eternal or originated? Whichever answer they give, it leads to a contradiction with their own beliefs or to theological absurdity. This passage demonstrates the power of logical refutation in kalam.

Guided Path
1
Understand the dilemma
The author presents two options for the nature of qudra: it must be either pre-eternal or originated. Recognize that this is a forced choice.
This sets up the entire refutation.
2
Explore the first horn: originated qudra
If qudra is originated, then in pre-eternity God would have been devoid of power (incapable). This implies God had a quality of incapability, which is a sign of origination. Following this logic leads to the conclusion that God Himself would be originated, which is impossible.
The author also notes that affirming originated qudra contradicts the Karamiyya's own doctrine.
3
Explore the second horn: pre-eternal qudra
If qudra is pre-eternal, does its pre-eternity necessitate the pre-eternity of that which it brings into existence (i.e., takwin)? The author forces them to answer yes or no.
Both answers lead to problems.
4
See the result: both horns refute the Karamiyya
If they say yes, then takwin is pre-eternal, contradicting their claim that it is originated. If they say no, they undermine their own principle that the pre-eternity of what the world depends on necessitates the pre-eternity of the world.
Thus the Karamiyya cannot consistently maintain their position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم نقول للكرامية : إن التكوين الحادث في ذات الله تعالى الذي تعلق حدوثه بالقدرة، أقديمة عندكم القدرة أم حادثه؟ فإن قالوا: حادثة، فقد تركوا مذهبهم ووصفوا الله تعالى في الأزل بالعجز وهو من أمارات الحدوث فجعلوه في الأزل مقرونا بسمات الحدث، فإن كان محدثا فقد أثبتوا حدوث الصانع مع أنه قول متناقض إذ القول بالحدوث في القدم محال، ولو كان قديما مع اقتران سمات الحدث به لكان العالم أيضا قديما وإن اقترنت به سمات الحدث مع أن هذا إبطال دليل الحدوث، حيث أثبتوا القدم مع دليل الحدوث. وإن قالوا: القدرة أزلية قيل لهم : هل أوجب قدمها قدم ما تعلق وجوده بها؟ فإن قالوا: نعم، فقد أقروا بقدم التكوين وتركوا مذهبهم. وإن قالوا: لا، أبطلوا كلامهم أن قدم ما يتعلق به وجود العالم يوجب قدم العالم.
Then we say to the Karamiyya: Indeed takwin, which is originated in the essence of Allah Most High, and whose origination is attached to qudra (power) – is qudra pre-eternal according to you or originated? If they say: originated, then they have abandoned their doctrine and described Allah Most High in pre-eternity as incapable, which is one of the signs of origination, so they have made Him in pre-eternity accompanied by signs of eventuality. For if He is originated, they have affirmed the origination of the Maker, although it is a contradictory statement because the statement of origination in pre-eternity is impossible. And if He were pre-eternal while accompanied by signs of eventuality, then the world would also be pre-eternal even if accompanied by signs of eventuality, although this is an invalidation of the proof of origination, since they have affirmed pre-eternity along with the proof of origination. And if they say: qudra is pre-eternal, it is said to them: Did its pre-eternity necessitate the pre-eternity of that whose existence is attached to it? If they say: yes, then they have admitted the pre-eternity of takwin and abandoned their doctrine. And if they say: no, they have invalidated their statement that the pre-eternity of that to which the existence of the world is attached necessitates the pre-eternity of the world.
Source pages p. 563

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Karamiyya sect specifically. The author addresses their claim about takwin (the attribute of bringing into existence) being originated in God's essence and attached to qudra (power). He poses a dilemma: is qudra pre-eternal or originated? If they say originated, they abandon their own doctrine and attribute inability to God in pre-eternity, which is contradictory because origination cannot be in pre-eternity; if God were pre-eternal yet bearing signs of origination, the world too could be pre-eternal despite signs of origination, undermining the proof of the world's origination. If they say qudra is pre-eternal, then they must answer whether that pre-eternity necessitates the pre-eternity of what is attached to it (i.e., the things created by takwin). If yes, they admit takwin is pre-eternal and abandon their doctrine. If no, they invalidate their own principle that the pre-eternity of what the world depends on necessitates the pre-eternity of the world. Thus the Karamiyya are caught in an inconsistent position.

Key Terms
التكوين
القدرة
القدم
الحدوث
الكرامية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that if qudra is pre-eternal, then necessarily takwin must be pre-eternal.
Correction: The author shows that this belief leads to a dilemma: affirming the necessity leads to contradicting the Karamiyya's claim that takwin is originated; denying it invalidates their own proof. Thus the Karamiyya cannot consistently hold their position.

Checkpoint
What is the first option the author presents to the Karamiyya regarding qudra?
A) Qudra is pre-eternal.
B) Qudra is originated.
C) Qudra is a divine attribute.
D) Qudra is identical with takwin.

Key Takeaway
The Karamiyya are trapped in a logical dilemma: whether qudra is originated or pre-eternal, each leads to a contradiction with their own principles or to theological absurdity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Karamiyya clung to their doctrine even when it led to logical absurdities. Are there any beliefs you hold about Allah that you have never subjected to critical examination? What would it mean for you to be wrong? Will you ask Allah to guide you to the truth, even if it upsets comfortable assumptions?
?
This dilemma shows that human reasoning, when separated from revelation, can trap us in contradictions. When you encounter a tension in your understanding of God's attributes, do you humbly submit to the limits of your intellect, or do you force a solution to maintain your preferred view? Which response brings you closer to Allah's pleasure?
?
The author's refutation is a form of intellectual jihad for the truth. Have you ever defended a truth about Allah even when it was difficult? Or have you remained silent to avoid conflict? Examine your heart: are you more concerned with being right or with submitting to what is right?

The Trilemma Against Mu'tazila and Najjariyya
Author refutes Mu'tazila and Najjariyya with a trilemma.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author refutes the Mu'tazila and Najjariyya by showing that their position on the world's dependence on God leads to the conclusion of the world's pre-eternity, which they deny.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazila and Najjariyya cannot escape the conclusion that the world is pre-eternal.

This passage presents a powerful logical refutation of two theological sects. The author forces them into a trilemma: either the world is attached to God's essence (making it pre-eternal), or they deny that (invalidating their proof), or they cut the attachment entirely (making the world independent and thus pre-eternal). We'll examine each branch.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then the translation. Notice the conditional structure: 'if... then...' repeated three times.
The author uses the same pattern for each horn of the trilemma.
2
Identify the three options
Find the three conditional statements. Each begins with 'إن' (if). Write them down in order.
The options are mutually exclusive.
3
Understand why each leads to pre-eternity
For each option, trace the reasoning: if attached to essence → pre-eternal; if deny attachment → proof collapses; if no attachment → world independent → pre-eternal.
The conclusion is the same: the world ends up pre-eternal.
4
Reflect on the rhetorical force
Ask yourself why this refutation is effective. It corners the opponent into admitting their own position implies what they deny.
This is a classic reductio ad absurdum.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذا المعتلة والنجارية يقولون: العالم مقدور الله تعالى وهو قادر لذاته، فإن تعلق وجوده بذاته الذي هو قادر به فقد أقروا على قضية كلامهم بقدم العالم إذ ذاته قديم، وإن امتنعوا عن القول بقدمه، أبطلوا دليلهم، وإن قالوا: وجود العالم غير متعلق بذاته ولا صفة الله تعالى يتعلق بها وجود العالم. فإذا وجود العالم لا بالله تعالى، وما لا تعلق لوجوده بغيره فهو قديم فإذا هم القائلون بقدم العالم.
And likewise the Mu'tazila and the Najjariyya say: The world is empowered (maqdur) by Allah Most High, and He is powerful (qadir) by His essence. So if its existence is attached to His essence by which He is powerful, then they have admitted, by the requirement of their statement, the pre-eternity of the world, since His essence is pre-eternal. And if they refrain from saying it is pre-eternal, they invalidate their proof. And if they say: The existence of the world is not attached to His essence nor to an attribute of Allah Most High by which the existence of the world is attached, then the existence of the world is not by Allah Most High; and whatever has no attachment of its existence to other than itself is pre-eternal – so then they are the ones who say the world is pre-eternal.
Source pages p. 563

Commentary
This passage refutes the Mu'tazila and Najjariyya sects regarding the dependence of the world's existence on God. These groups affirm that the world is maqdur (empowered) by God, and that God is qadir (powerful) by His essence. The author presents a trilemma. First, if they say the world's existence is attached to God's essence (by which He is powerful), then consistency forces them to admit the world's pre-eternity because God's essence is pre-eternal—so whatever depends on that essence would also be pre-eternal. Second, if they deny the world's pre-eternity, they invalidate their own proof that the world is dependent on a pre-eternal essence. Third, if they say the world's existence is not attached to God's essence nor to any attribute of God, then the world's existence is not from God at all; and anything independent in existence is pre-eternal—so again they end up affirming the world's pre-eternity. Thus they are caught in a contradiction no matter which position they take.

Key Terms
المقدور
القادر
الذات
القدم
المعتزلة
النجارية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that affirming God's power over the world does not require the world to be pre-eternal.
Correction: The author shows that if the attachment is to God's essence (which is pre-eternal), then the world must also be pre-eternal.

Checkpoint
What is the third option the author presents to the Mu'tazila and Najjariyya?
A) The world's existence is attached to God's essence.
B) The world's existence is attached to an attribute of God.
C) The world's existence is not attached to God's essence nor to any attribute.
D) The world's existence is pre-eternal by itself.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila and Najjariyya cannot consistently affirm the world's dependence on a pre-eternal God without also affirming the world's pre-eternity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Mu'tazila tried to hold two positions that led to contradiction. Is there an area of your faith where you avoid following a belief to its logical end because it would force you to change something comfortable? What would it cost you to be fully consistent?
?
The third option—living as if your existence is not attached to God—leads to the claim of independence. In what ways do you act as though your life is self-sufficient, needing no attachment to God's attributes? How would your day change if you consciously lived in constant 'attachment' to His essence?
?
If the world's pre-eternity is unacceptable, yet the alternative is to invalidate your own proof, which will you choose? This lesson demands that you either affirm the world's dependence on God or reject it. Have you ever examined whether your daily reliance on God is real or merely theoretical? What step can you take today to make that reliance tangible?

The Ash'ari Dilemma: Eternal Command Leading to Eternity of the World
Nasafi presents a dialectical argument against the Ash'aris.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi uses the Ash'aris' own admission about the eternal command 'Kun' to argue that their position leads to either embracing the eternity of the world or contradicting their own principles.

Core Idea
The eternal 'Kun' forces the Ash'aris into a dilemma: eternal world or self-contradiction.

Nasafi begins his refutation by engaging the Ash'aris on their own grounds. He points out that if they accept that the world was created by the eternal address 'Kun', then they must logically accept that the world is eternal, since the cause is eternal. If they deny this, they invalidate their own claim. This dialectical move sets up the central challenge to the Ash'ari position.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let Nasafi's own dialectical rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the conditional structure: 'If they say yes... then...'.
2
Identify the dilemma
Nasafi presents two options for the Ash'aris based on their admission. Find both branches and understand the consequence of each.
3
Reflect on the implications
Consider why these consequences are devastating for the Ash'ari position: one leads to disbelief, the other to inconsistency.
This connects to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم ننتقل إلى الأشعرية فنقول لهم: أليس حدوث العالم كان بخطاب "كن" إذ أقررتم بأجمعكم أن الله تعالى خلق العالم بخطاب "كن" على ما سبق من تقرير مذهبكم في ذلك. فإن قالوا: بلى ولابد منه. قيل: فإذا أنتم على زعمكم واقتضاء كلامكم قائلون بقدم العالم حيث أثبتم تعلقه بما هو قديم في نفسه. فإن أقروا به كفروا والتحقوا بالدهرية، وإن أنكروا، أبطلوا كلامهم. فزعم هذا الذي ذكر قولنا مع قول ابن قلس حيث أورد هذا الكلام على نفسه، والحماقة والوقاحة وقصد التلبيس على الضعفة لما تكلم بمثل هذا الكلام الذي يقرر كلام خصومه ويهدم جميع قواعده، وذلك لأن أكثر ما في الباب أنه لا يسمى الكلام الأزلي تكوينا، بل يسمى المخلوق تكوينا، ولكنه أقر أن القول الأزلي يحصل به التكوين وهو عنده المكون فصار المكون المخلوق حاصلا بالقول الأزلي. ونحن لا ندعي إلا هذا، فإنا نقول الله تعالى صفة أزلية يحصل بها المخلوقات. وهذا قد أعطى هذا المعنى حيث قال: التكوين الذي هو المكون عنده يحصل بكلامه الأزلي، وقدم كلامه الأزلي لم يوجب قدم ما يحصل به إلا أنا نسميه تكوينا وفعلا وهو لا يسميه وإن حصل به المكون، ويسمى التكوين نفس المكون، ونفسه لا يحصل بنفسه فامتنع عن تسمية ما يحصل به التكون والوجود، إيجادًا أو تكوينا، (وسمي ما لم يحصل به المكون والوجود إيجادا وتكوينا) وهو خطأ في اللغة، فصار مساعدا لخصمه في المعنى، مسلما له ما يدعي من الحقيقة هادما دليله بالمساعدة خصمه ناسبا نفسه إلى القول بقدم العالم على زعمه ثم صار مخالفا خصمه في التسمية والعبارة، ولا عبرة بها مع المساعدة في المعنى. ثم مخبطا فيما زعم عند أرباب اللغة. على أن قدم التكوين لو أوجب قدم المكون مع أنه محال على ما مر، لأوجب لو كان التكوين ليكون المكون في الأزل، فأما إذا كان التكوين لتكون في الوقت الذي علم حدوثه وأراد لم يكن التكوين موجبا قدم المكون هذا كما أن الإرادة بلا خلاف بيننا وبين الأشعرية أزلية، وقدمها لا يوجب قدم المراد، لما أنه لم يرد بها كون المراد في الأزل، بل أراد كونه في وقت وجوده، فكذا هذا، وكذا قوله كن، وإن كان أزليا لم يوجب قدم العالم لهذا. وهذا هو الجواب عن قولهم: إن
Then we turn to the Ash'aris and say to them: Was not the coming into existence of the world by the address "Kun", since you all acknowledge that Allah created the world by the address "Kun" according to what has preceded of the presentation of your doctrine in that regard? If they say: Yes, and it is necessary. It is said: Then you, according to your claim and the implication of your statement, are saying the world is eternal, since you have affirmed its relation to what is eternal in itself. If they admit that, they disbelieve and join the materialists (Dahriyya); and if they deny it, they invalidate their own statement. He claimed that this which he mentioned is our statement along with the statement of Ibn Qalls when he directed this speech against himself, and foolishness, shamelessness, and intent to deceive the weak, when he spoke such speech which confirms the speech of his opponents and demolishes all his foundations. That is because the most of the matter is that he does not call the eternal speech takwin (bringing into existence), but rather calls the created thing takwin; but he acknowledged that the eternal speech brings about takwin, and in his view it is the made thing, so the created made thing occurs by the eternal speech. And we claim nothing but this: we say that Allah has an eternal attribute by which creatures occur. And this one has granted this meaning when he said: The takwin, which is the made thing in his view, occurs by His eternal speech, and the eternity of His eternal speech does not necessitate the eternity of what occurs by it; except that we call it takwin and act, while he does not call it that, even though the made thing occurs by it. And he calls takwin the same as the made thing, and the thing itself does not occur by itself; so he refrained from calling what brings about takwin and existence an act of bringing into existence or takwin, and he called what does not bring about the made thing and existence an act of bringing into existence and takwin, which is an error in language. So he becomes an aid to his opponent in meaning, conceding to him what he claims of the reality, demolishing his own proof by aiding his opponent, attributing himself to the statement that the world is eternal, according to his claim; then he becomes opposed to his opponent in naming and expression, and no regard is paid to that along with aid in meaning. Then he is confused, in his claim, in the view of linguists. However, if the eternity of takwin necessitated the eternity of the made thing—though it is impossible as has passed—it would necessitate if the takwin were in order that the made thing be in pre-eternity. But if the takwin were in order that it be at the time He knew its occurrence and willed, the takwin would not necessitate the eternity of the made thing. This is like the will, without disagreement between us and the Ash'aris, being eternal; its eternity does not necessitate the eternity of the willed, because He did not will by it that the willed be in pre-eternity, but He willed its being at the time of its existence; so likewise this one, and likewise His statement "Kun", even though it is eternal, does not necessitate the eternity of the world for this reason. And this is the answer to their statement: Indeed
Source pages p. 564

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Ash'ari position regarding the eternal command 'Kun'. The author begins by presenting the Ash'ari claim that the world's creation occurred by the eternal address 'Kun'. He then argues that if the Ash'aris admit this, they must logically admit the eternity of the world because the address is eternal and the world is related to it. If they deny this, they contradict themselves; if they admit it, they become like the materialists. The author then criticizes an Ash'ari opponent (possibly Ibn Qalls) for trying to evade this by claiming that the eternal speech is not called takwin (bringing into existence) but rather the created effect is called takwin. The author points out that this opponent nevertheless concedes that the eternal speech brings about the created thing, which is exactly what the Maturidis claim—that Allah has an eternal attribute by which creatures occur. The author argues that the opponent's terminological distinction is merely verbal and does not affect the underlying reality, and that it violates linguistic norms. The author then provides a key analogy: the eternal will (irada) does not necessitate the eternity of the willed thing because the will is for the thing to be at a specific time, not in pre-eternity. Similarly, the eternal command 'Kun' is for the world to be at the time of its creation, not eternally. Thus, the eternity of the command does not entail the eternity of the world. The passage ends mid-sentence but the argument is essentially complete.

Key Terms
خطاب كن
قدم العالم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think Nasafi is merely attacking terminology; actually he is exposing logical consequences.
Correction: Nasafi's argument is logical: from the Ash'aris' own premises, a necessary conclusion follows, regardless of terminology.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, what follows if the Ash'aris admit that the world was created by the eternal command 'Kun'?
A) They must admit the world is eternal.
B) They prove the command is temporal.
C) They are consistent.
D) They avoid disbelief.

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari belief in an eternal creative command logically entails the eternity of the world, a conclusion they must either accept (leading to disbelief) or reject (undermining their own position).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Ash'aris were trapped by their own belief about 'Kun.' Are you willing to examine your own deeply held beliefs, even if it means facing uncomfortable logical consequences? Will you seek truth even at the cost of your pride?
?
Nasafi's argument forced a choice between admitting error or accepting disbelief. Have you ever clung to a belief that, if followed honestly, would lead you away from Islam? This lesson calls you to be ruthlessly honest with yourself—will you?
?
If you accept that Allah's attribute of speech is eternal, do you see how your belief about creation must align with that? Or do you hold contradictions without realizing it? Commit today to studying the logical implications of what you believe about Allah's attributes.

Terminological Evasion: Why Calling Eternal Speech 'Not Takwin' Fails
Nasafi analyzes and refutes an Ash'ari terminological distinction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Nasafi's critique of the Ash'ari attempt to avoid the dilemma by distinguishing between eternal speech and takwin.

Core Idea
The opponent's terminological trick concedes the substance: eternal speech brings about creation.

After presenting the dilemma, Nasafi addresses an Ash'ari counterargument that tries to avoid the implication by claiming that the eternal speech is not called takwin (bringing into existence) but the created effect is. Nasafi shows that this opponent actually admits that the eternal speech brings about the created thing, which is exactly the Maturidi position. The verbal distinction does not change the reality.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the opponent's claim and Nasafi's rebuttal.
Pay attention to the terms 'takwin' and 'mukawwan'.
2
Identify the opponent's concession
Nasafi argues that the opponent admits the eternal speech brings about the created thing. Find the sentence that shows this.
3
Understand why terminology is secondary
Nasafi says the opponent aids his opponent in meaning. Reflect on why the verbal difference does not matter if the reality is the same.
Consider the linguistic error Nasafi points out.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

In your own life, is there a sin or shortcoming you have renamed—calling it a 'struggle' instead of disobedience, a 'personality trait' instead of arrogance—to avoid repenting? Are you willing to call it what Allah calls it, even if it costs your comfort?
?
Nasafi says 'no regard is paid to naming along with aid in meaning.' When you argue with others about religion, do you focus more on winning the verbal dispute or on the heart of the matter? If you found your opponent concedes the truth, would you still insist they use your terminology as a condition? Search your last disagreement—was it about a word or a reality?
?

What subtle shifts in your speech have you made to rationalize your complacency in deeds? Today, ask Allah to correct your tongue before your heart.

The Analogy of the Eternal Will: Why Eternal Command Does Not Entail Eternity
Nasafi presents an analogy to defend the Maturidi position.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Nasafi's analogy between the eternal command 'Kun' and the eternal will, and how it refutes the Ash'ari objection.

Core Idea
Just as the eternal will does not necessitate the eternity of the willed, the eternal command does not necessitate the eternity of the world.

Nasafi concludes his refutation by providing a powerful analogy. He notes that both the Maturidis and Ash'aris agree that the divine will is eternal, yet that does not make the willed object eternal—because the will is for the object to exist at a specific time. Similarly, the eternal command 'Kun' is for the world to come into existence at its destined time, not in pre-eternity. Therefore, the eternity of the command does not imply the eternity of the world.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Note the structure: condition, analogy, application.
The passage ends mid-sentence, but the main analogy is complete.
2
Understand the logic of the analogy
Nasafi compares the eternal command to the eternal will. Grasp why the eternity of the will does not necessitate the eternity of the willed.
The key: the will is for a specific time, not for pre-eternity.
3
Apply the analogy to the command
Similarly, the command 'Kun' is for the world to be at its time of creation. Therefore, the eternity of the command does not make the world eternal.
This directly answers the Ash'ari objection.

ثم ننتقل إلى الأشعرية فنقول لهم: أليس حدوث العالم كان بخطاب "كن" إذ أقررتم بأجمعكم أن الله تعالى خلق العالم بخطاب "كن" على ما سبق من تقرير مذهبكم في ذلك. فإن قالوا: بلى ولابد منه. قيل: فإذا أنتم على زعمكم واقتضاء كلامكم قائلون بقدم العالم حيث أثبتم تعلقه بما هو قديم في نفسه. فإن أقروا به كفروا والتحقوا بالدهرية، وإن أنكروا، أبطلوا كلامهم. فزعم هذا الذي ذكر قولنا مع قول ابن قلس حيث أورد هذا الكلام على نفسه، والحماقة والوقاحة وقصد التلبيس على الضعفة لما تكلم بمثل هذا الكلام الذي يقرر كلام خصومه ويهدم جميع قواعده، وذلك لأن أكثر ما في الباب أنه لا يسمى الكلام الأزلي تكوينا، بل يسمى المخلوق تكوينا، ولكنه أقر أن القول الأزلي يحصل به التكوين وهو عنده المكون فصار المكون المخلوق حاصلا بالقول الأزلي. ونحن لا ندعي إلا هذا، فإنا نقول الله تعالى صفة أزلية يحصل بها المخلوقات. وهذا قد أعطى هذا المعنى حيث قال: التكوين الذي هو المكون عنده يحصل بكلامه الأزلي، وقدم كلامه الأزلي لم يوجب قدم ما يحصل به إلا أنا نسميه تكوينا وفعلا وهو لا يسميه وإن حصل به المكون، ويسمى التكوين نفس المكون، ونفسه لا يحصل بنفسه فامتنع عن تسمية ما يحصل به التكون والوجود، إيجادًا أو تكوينا، (وسمي ما لم يحصل به المكون والوجود إيجادا وتكوينا) وهو خطأ في اللغة، فصار مساعدا لخصمه في المعنى، مسلما له ما يدعي من الحقيقة هادما دليله بالمساعدة خصمه ناسبا نفسه إلى القول بقدم العالم على زعمه ثم صار مخالفا خصمه في التسمية والعبارة، ولا عبرة بها مع المساعدة في المعنى. ثم مخبطا فيما زعم عند أرباب اللغة. على أن قدم التكوين لو أوجب قدم المكون مع أنه محال على ما مر، لأوجب لو كان التكوين ليكون المكون في الأزل، فأما إذا كان التكوين لتكون في الوقت الذي علم حدوثه وأراد لم يكن التكوين موجبا قدم المكون هذا كما أن الإرادة بلا خلاف بيننا وبين الأشعرية أزلية، وقدمها لا يوجب قدم المراد، لما أنه لم يرد بها كون المراد في الأزل، بل أراد كونه في وقت وجوده، فكذا هذا، وكذا قوله كن، وإن كان أزليا لم يوجب قدم العالم لهذا. وهذا هو الجواب عن قولهم: إن
Then we turn to the Ash'aris and say to them: Was not the coming into existence of the world by the address "Kun", since you all acknowledge that Allah created the world by the address "Kun" according to what has preceded of the presentation of your doctrine in that regard? If they say: Yes, and it is necessary. It is said: Then you, according to your claim and the implication of your statement, are saying the world is eternal, since you have affirmed its relation to what is eternal in itself. If they admit that, they disbelieve and join the materialists (Dahriyya); and if they deny it, they invalidate their own statement. He claimed that this which he mentioned is our statement along with the statement of Ibn Qalls when he directed this speech against himself, and foolishness, shamelessness, and intent to deceive the weak, when he spoke such speech which confirms the speech of his opponents and demolishes all his foundations. That is because the most of the matter is that he does not call the eternal speech takwin (bringing into existence), but rather calls the created thing takwin; but he acknowledged that the eternal speech brings about takwin, and in his view it is the made thing, so the created made thing occurs by the eternal speech. And we claim nothing but this: we say that Allah has an eternal attribute by which creatures occur. And this one has granted this meaning when he said: The takwin, which is the made thing in his view, occurs by His eternal speech, and the eternity of His eternal speech does not necessitate the eternity of what occurs by it; except that we call it takwin and act, while he does not call it that, even though the made thing occurs by it. And he calls takwin the same as the made thing, and the thing itself does not occur by itself; so he refrained from calling what brings about takwin and existence an act of bringing into existence or takwin, and he called what does not bring about the made thing and existence an act of bringing into existence and takwin, which is an error in language. So he becomes an aid to his opponent in meaning, conceding to him what he claims of the reality, demolishing his own proof by aiding his opponent, attributing himself to the statement that the world is eternal, according to his claim; then he becomes opposed to his opponent in naming and expression, and no regard is paid to that along with aid in meaning. Then he is confused, in his claim, in the view of linguists. However, if the eternity of takwin necessitated the eternity of the made thing—though it is impossible as has passed—it would necessitate if the takwin were in order that the made thing be in pre-eternity. But if the takwin were in order that it be at the time He knew its occurrence and willed, the takwin would not necessitate the eternity of the made thing. This is like the will, without disagreement between us and the Ash'aris, being eternal; its eternity does not necessitate the eternity of the willed, because He did not will by it that the willed be in pre-eternity, but He willed its being at the time of its existence; so likewise this one, and likewise His statement "Kun", even though it is eternal, does not necessitate the eternity of the world for this reason. And this is the answer to their statement: Indeed
Source pages p. 564

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Ash'ari position regarding the eternal command 'Kun'. The author begins by presenting the Ash'ari claim that the world's creation occurred by the eternal address 'Kun'. He then argues that if the Ash'aris admit this, they must logically admit the eternity of the world because the address is eternal and the world is related to it. If they deny this, they contradict themselves; if they admit it, they become like the materialists. The author then criticizes an Ash'ari opponent (possibly Ibn Qalls) for trying to evade this by claiming that the eternal speech is not called takwin (bringing into existence) but rather the created effect is called takwin. The author points out that this opponent nevertheless concedes that the eternal speech brings about the created thing, which is exactly what the Maturidis claim—that Allah has an eternal attribute by which creatures occur. The author argues that the opponent's terminological distinction is merely verbal and does not affect the underlying reality, and that it violates linguistic norms. The author then provides a key analogy: the eternal will (irada) does not necessitate the eternity of the willed thing because the will is for the thing to be at a specific time, not in pre-eternity. Similarly, the eternal command 'Kun' is for the world to be at the time of its creation, not eternally. Thus, the eternity of the command does not entail the eternity of the world. The passage ends mid-sentence but the argument is essentially complete.

Key Terms
إرادة
مراد
تكوين
خطاب كن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the analogy fails because will and command are different; Nasafi shows they function similarly in this context.
Correction: Nasafi's analogy is valid because both will and command are eternal attributes that are directed at temporal effects.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, why does the eternal command 'Kun' not necessitate the eternity of the world?
A) Because the command is not truly eternal.
B) Because the command is for the world to be at a specific time, analogous to the eternal will.
C) Because the world is created by a temporal command.
D) Because the Ash'aris deny the command.

Key Takeaway
The eternity of a cause does not imply the eternity of its effect if the cause is directed at producing the effect at a specific time.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever feel trapped by the thought that because God's will is eternal, your past sins are eternally decreed beyond change? How does Nasafi's argument that the eternal will is directed at the time of existence free you to seek forgiveness in the present moment?
?
If God's command 'Be' is eternal, yet the world is not eternal, what does that tell you about the nature of God's speech and your own relationship with time? How does this affect the way you wait for God's timing in your life?
?
When you reflect on your own decisions, do you assume that because a desire is strong it must be fulfilled? How does the distinction between an eternal cause and a temporal effect challenge you to trust God's wisdom in delaying or withholding what you want?

Refutation of the Ash'ari Conflation of Takwin with the Created Thing
Imam al-Nasafi refutes the Ash'ari claim that takwin is the created thing itself, showing it leads to contradiction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Imam al-Nasafi argues that the Ash'ari position on takwin is self-defeating and amounts to a verbal difference that concedes the Maturidi understanding.

Core Idea
The Ash'ari's refusal to call eternal speech 'takwin' is a verbal trick that hides agreement in meaning.

In this passage, Imam al-Nasafi dismantles the Ash'ari claim that takwin is identical to the created thing. He exposes the logical and linguistic contradictions in their position, showing that they inadvertently concede the Maturidi view that an eternal attribute brings creation into existence. The lesson will guide you through his refutation step by step.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Ash'ari position on takwin
The Ash'ari says takwin is the created thing itself, not an eternal attribute. But they admit takwin occurs through eternal speech. Notice the contradiction.
This concession is key to al-Nasafi's refutation.
2
Follow al-Nasafi's exposure of the error
He points out that calling the created thing 'takwin' leads to absurdity because a thing cannot bring itself into existence. Also, this is a linguistic mistake.
3
Analyze the argument about pre-eternity
Al-Nasafi shows that even if takwin were considered eternal, it does not necessitate the pre-eternity of the created thing, because takwin is for a specific time, not for pre-eternity.
This addresses the charge that takwin without a mukawwan implies incapacity.
4
Compare with the attribute of will
Just as eternal will does not make the willed object eternal, eternal takwin does not make the mukawwan eternal. This refutes the objection.
The analogy with will (irada) is a standard Maturidi argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والحماقة والوقاحة وقصد التلبيس على الضعفة لما تكلم بمثل هذا الكلام الذي يقرر كلام خصومه ويهدم جميع قواعده، وذلك لأن أكثر ما في الباب أنه لا يسمى الكلام الأزلي تكوينا، بل يسمى المخلوق تكوينا، ولكنه أقر أن القول الأزلي يحصل به التكوين وهو عنده المكون فصار المكون المخلوق حاصلا بالقول الأزلي. ونحن لا ندعي إلا هذا، فإنا نقول الله تعالى صفة أزلية يحصل بها المخلوقات. وهذا قد أعطى هذا المعنى حيث قال: التكوين الذي هو المكون عنده يحصل بكلامه الأزلي، وقدم كلامه الأزلي لم يوجب قدم ما يحصل به إلا أنا نسميه تكوينا وفعلا وهو لا يسميه وإن حصل به المكون ، ويسمى التكوين نفس المكون، ونفسه لا يحصل بنفسه فامتنع عن تسمية ما يحصل به التكون والوجود، إيجادا أو تكوينا، وسمى ما لم يحصل به المكون والوجود إيجادا وتكوينا وهو خطأ في اللغة، فصار مساعدا لخصمه في المعنى، مسلما له ما يدعي من الحقيقة هادما دليله بالمساعدة خصمه ناسبا نفسه إلى القول بقدم العالم على زعمه ثم صار مخالفا خصمه في التسمية والعبارة، ولا عبرة بها مع المساعدة في المعنى. ثم مخبطا فيما زعم عند أرباب اللغة. على أن قدم التكوين لو أوجب قدم المكون مع أنه محال على ما مر، لأوجب لو كان التكوين ليكون المكون في الأزل، فأما إذا كان التكوين لتكون في الوقت الذي علم حدوثه وأراد لم يكن التكوين موجبا قدم المكون هذا كما أن الإرادة بلا خلاف بيننا وبين الأشعرية أزلية، وقدمها لا يوجب قدم المراد، لما أنه لم يرد بها كون المراد في الأزل، بل أراد كونه في وقت وجوده، فكذا هذا، وكذا قوله كن، وإن كان أزليا لم يوجب قدم العالم لهذا. وهذا هو الجواب عن قولهم: إن التكوين ولا مكون عجز. قلنا: إنما يكون كذلك أن لو وجد التكوين ليكون المكون القدم، فلم يكن، وما كان التكوين لهذا بل ليوجد في وقته. ألا ترى أنه لا يقال وجود الإرادة ولا مراد عجز و اضطرار، لأنه إنما يكون كذلك أن لو كانت الإرادة ليكون المراد في الأزل فلم يكن ، فأما إذا كانت ليكون المراد في وقته، لم يلزم بعد المراد في الأزل ضرورة وعجز ، فكذا هذا.
And [this is] foolishness, shamelessness, and the intention to deceive the weak, when he speaks such speech that affirms the words of his opponents and destroys all his principles. This is because most of what is in the chapter is that he does not call the eternal speech takwin, rather he calls the created thing takwin, but he affirmed that the eternal saying produces takwin, and in his view it is the mukawwan, so the created mukawwan comes to be by the eternal saying. And we claim nothing but this, for we say: Allah Most High has an eternal attribute by which created things come to be. And this [opponent] has granted this meaning when he said: 'Takwin, which in his view is the mukawwan, occurs by His eternal speech.' And the pre-eternity of His eternal speech does not necessitate the pre-eternity of that by which it occurs, except that we call it takwin and act (fi'l), while he does not call it that, even though the mukawwan occurs by it. And he calls takwin the very mukawwan, but a thing itself does not come to be by itself, so he refrains from naming that by which occurrence and existence come to be as 'bringing into existence' or 'takwin', and he names that by which the mukawwan and existence do not occur as 'bringing into existence' and 'takwin' — and this is an error in language. Thus he becomes an assistant to his opponent in meaning, conceding to him what he claims of the reality, destroying his own argument by assisting his opponent, attributing himself to the statement of the pre-eternity of the world according to his assumption, then he becomes an opponent to his opponent in naming and expression, and no attention is paid to that while he assists in meaning. Then he is confused, according to his claim, among the masters of language. However, if the pre-eternity of takwin necessitated the pre-eternity of the mukawwan — though it is impossible as has passed — then it would necessitate if takwin existed to make the mukawwan pre-eternal. But if takwin is to bring about [the mukawwan] at the time that [God] knew its temporality and willed, then takwin does not necessitate the pre-eternity of the mukawwan. This is like the case of will (al-irada): without dispute between us and the Ash'ariyya, it is pre-eternal, and its pre-eternity does not necessitate the pre-eternity of the willed object, because He did not will by it the existence of the willed object in pre-eternity, but rather He willed its existence at the time of its occurrence. So likewise this, and likewise His saying 'Kun', even if it is pre-eternal, does not necessitate the pre-eternity of the world for this reason. And this is the answer to their saying: 'Takwin without a mukawwan implies incapacity.' We say: That would only be the case if takwin existed to make the mukawwan pre-eternal, but it was not so; rather, takwin is for this [i.e., to bring it about at its time], but to make it exist at its time. Do you not see that it is not said: 'Existence of will without a willed object implies incapacity and constraint', because that would only be the case if will existed to make the willed object pre-eternal, but it was not so. But if it is to make the willed object at its time, then the absence of the willed object in pre-eternity does not necessitate necessity and incapacity. So likewise this.
Source pages p. 565

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an Ash'ari argument regarding the attribute of takwin (bringing into existence). The Imam accuses his opponent of foolishness and dishonesty for advancing an argument that actually supports the Maturidi position and destroys his own principles. The core issue is that the Ash'ari refuses to call the eternal speech (kalam azali) 'takwin', but instead calls the created thing (mukhlaq) 'takwin'. However, he admits that the eternal speech produces takwin, which in his view is the mukawwan. Thus, the created mukawwan comes about through the eternal speech. The Imam points out that this cedes the point: the Maturidis claim there is an eternal attribute by which creatures come into being. The Ash'ari, despite his terminology, concedes this reality. The difference is merely verbal. The Imam then elaborates that calling takwin the very same as the mukawwan is absurd, as a thing cannot bring itself into existence, and this is a linguistic error. Addressing the issue of pre-eternity: if takwin were eternal, would that imply the pre-eternity of the mukawwan? No, because takwin is intended to create the thing at the time known to God, not in pre-eternity. He analogizes with divine will (irada), which is eternal but does not necessitate the pre-eternity of the willed object. Similarly, the command 'Kun' is eternal but does not necessitate the pre-eternity of the world. This is the answer to the Ash'ari's claim that 'takwin without a mukawwan implies incapacity'. The Imam responds that this would only hold if takwin were meant to create in pre-eternity, but it is meant for the appointed time. Just as with will, it is not said that will exists without a willed object implies incapacity, because will is for a specific time.

Key Terms
التكوين (takwin)
المكون (mukawwan)
الكلام الأزلي (al-kalam al-azali)
الإرادة (al-irada)
قدم (qidam)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If takwin is eternal, then the created thing must also be eternal.
Correction: Takwin is eternal in the sense that the attribute is pre-eternal, but it is directed to bring about creatures at their appointed times, not in pre-eternity. Thus, pre-eternity of takwin does not entail pre-eternity of the mukawwan.

Checkpoint
According to Imam al-Nasafi, what is the key error in the Ash'ari's position on takwin?
A) He denies the existence of takwin altogether.
B) He calls the created thing 'takwin' rather than the eternal attribute, leading to a verbal difference that obscures agreement in meaning.
C) He claims that takwin is a created attribute.
D) He argues that takwin necessitates the pre-eternity of the world.

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari concession that takwin occurs through eternal speech actually supports the Maturidi view that a pre-eternal attribute brings about creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever used a different word for something to avoid admitting a truth you know in your heart? Can you identify one area in your faith where you are attached to a label rather than the reality it signifies, and what would it cost you to align your language with the truth?
?
When you debate matters of religion, do you genuinely seek to understand what your opponent is saying, or do you dismiss them because they use different terminology? Ask yourself: Are you more concerned with winning the argument or with arriving at the truth, even if it means your 'opponent' has a point?
?
The Ash'ari in this passage ended up destroying his own argument because he insisted on a verbal distinction while conceding the meaning. Are there beliefs or practices you hold onto merely because of the words you use, while in practice you have already conceded the core issue? What would it look like to let go of the false label and embrace the truth?
